

```python
# Project Description

# Project News Mood is a learning project on how to use the Vader Sentiment Analyze and Tweepy module in conjuction with Pandas and Matplotlib to analyze information from tweets.  

# The purpose of the project is to create a Python script to to perform a sentiment analysis of the Twitter activity of various news oulets, and to present your findings in a visual method.  
```


```python
#Directory:

# News_Mood.ipynb

# Overall Media Sentiment based on Twitter 03_24_18.png

# README.md

# Sentiment Analysis of Media Tweets 03_24_18.png

```


```python
#Observations

# 1. No observable trend for the sentiment analysis of media tweets scatter plot. 

# 2. CBS had the overall most positive sentiment for tweets while NY Times had the overall most negative sentiment for tweets.

# 3. It is interesting to note that Fox News has a slightly more positive overall tweet polarity than CNN. Not sure why this is
# the case. Perhaps it is only a conclusion from this particular dataset. 
```


```python
import tweepy
import json
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import seaborn as sb
import config
% matplotlib inline
```


```python
# Import and Initialize Sentiment Analyzer
from vaderSentiment.vaderSentiment import SentimentIntensityAnalyzer
analyzer = SentimentIntensityAnalyzer()
```


```python
# Setup Tweepy API Authentication
auth = tweepy.OAuthHandler(config.consumer_key, config.consumer_secret)
auth.set_access_token(config.access_token, config.access_token_secret)
api = tweepy.API(auth, parser=tweepy.parsers.JSONParser())
```


```python
# Target User Accounts
target_user = ("BBC", "CBS", "CNN", "FoxNews", "nytimes")



# Variables for holding sentiments
compound_list = []
positive_list = []
negative_list = []
neutral_list = []
news_sources_dictionary = {"compound": [], 
                           "positive": [], 
                           "negative": [], 
                           "neutral" : [], 
                           "source": [],
                           "date_created": [],
                           "text in tweet": [],
                          "counter":[]}
                           

# Loop through each user
for user in target_user:

    # Loop through 5 pages of tweets (total 100 tweets)
    for x in range(5):

        # Get all tweets from home feed (for each page specified)
        public_tweets = api.user_timeline(user, page=x)
        count = 0
        # Loop through all tweets
        for tweet in public_tweets:

            # Run Vader Analysis on each tweet
            compound = analyzer.polarity_scores(tweet["text"])["compound"]
            pos = analyzer.polarity_scores(tweet["text"])["pos"]
            neu = analyzer.polarity_scores(tweet["text"])["neu"]
            neg = analyzer.polarity_scores(tweet["text"])["neg"]

            # Add each value to the appropriate array
            news_sources_dictionary['compound'].append(compound)
            news_sources_dictionary["positive"].append(pos)
            news_sources_dictionary["negative"].append(neg)
            news_sources_dictionary["neutral"].append(neu)
            news_sources_dictionary["source"].append(tweet["user"]["name"])
            news_sources_dictionary["date_created"].append(tweet["created_at"])
            news_sources_dictionary["text in tweet"].append(tweet["text"])
            news_sources_dictionary["counter"].append(count)
            
            count+=1

print(news_sources_dictionary)
```

# Calculate the means for all sentiments for NY times

```python
# Create a sources averages list with the compound averages for each source as the elements of the list

news_sources_compound_averages_list = [bbc_comp_means[0], cbs_comp_means[0], cnn_comp_means[0], fox_news_means[0], nyt_comp_means[0]]
news_sources_compound_averages_list
```




    [0.05808799999999999, 0.364953, -0.072203, 0.045306, -0.01953300000000001]




```python
# Plot the Overall Media Sentiment bar graph

plt.figure(figsize=(20,9))

Ov_med_bar = plt.bar(x = np.arange(5), height = news_sources_compound_averages_list)
plt.label = New_sources_dict_df['source']
plt.title("Overall Media Sentiment based on Twitter (03/24/18)")

colors = ['r', 'g', 'b', 'orange', 'gold']

for i,color in enumerate(colors):
    
    Ov_med_bar[i].set_color(color)
    
plt.xticks(np.arange(5), [New_sources_dict_df['source'][0], New_sources_dict_df['source'][100], New_sources_dict_df['source'][200], New_sources_dict_df['source'][300], New_sources_dict_df['source'][400]]) 

#['a', 'b', 'c', 'd', 'e'])

plt.ylabel("Tweet Polarity")

# Save the figure
plt.savefig("Overall Media Sentiment based on Twitter 03_24_18.png")

plt.show()

```

```python
# filter our data to separate sources

source_BBC = New_sources_dict_df[New_sources_dict_df["source"] == "BBC"]
source_CBS = New_sources_dict_df[New_sources_dict_df["source"] == "CBS"]
source_CNN = New_sources_dict_df[New_sources_dict_df["source"] == "CNN"]
source_Fox_News = New_sources_dict_df[New_sources_dict_df["source"] == "Fox News"]
source_New_York_Times = New_sources_dict_df[New_sources_dict_df["source"] == "The New York Times"]
news = [source_BBC, source_CBS, source_CNN, source_Fox_News, source_New_York_Times]
```


```python
#Create the scatterplot for the Sentiment Analysis of Media Tweets

plt.figure(figsize=(20,9))
colors = ('r','b')

for i, df in enumerate(news):
    name = target_user[i]
    plt.scatter(x=df["counter"], y=df["compound"],label =name) #x=df["date_created"]

# Incorporate the other graph properties
plt.title("Sentiment Analysis of Media Tweets (03/24/18)")
plt.ylabel("Tweet Polarity")
plt.xlabel("Tweets Ago")
plt.grid(True)
plt.legend(loc='best')
# Save the figure
plt.savefig("Sentiment Analysis of Media Tweets 03_24_18.png")

# Show plot
plt.show()
```
